# Data Science Foundations: Fundamentals

> Data science is the collection of fields involved in artificial intelligence, machine learning, and business intelligence. It’s one of the fastest growing, most rewarding careers, employing analysts and engineers around the globe. This course provides an accessible, non-technical introduction to the field of data science, covering the vocabulary, skills, jobs, tools, and techniques of data science

> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071) | 5h 24m
> [Jump to Path Context ↓](#path-context)

## Table of Contents

- **1. Introduction** (1 videos)
- **2. 1. What Is Data Science?** (6 videos)
- **3. 2. The Place of Data Science in the Data Universe** (8 videos)
- **4. 3. Ethics, Privacy, and Regulation** (5 videos)
- **5. 4. Sources of Data and Insights** (11 videos)
- **6. 5. Tools and Techniques for Data Science** (5 videos)
- **7. 6. Math Foundations for Data Science** (5 videos)
- **8. 7. Learning Paradigms** (8 videos)
- **9. 8. Algorithms That Create** (2 videos)
- **10. 9. Acting on Data Science** (3 videos)
- **11. Conclusion** (1 videos)

>
> **[0:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/welcome?u=76281980&t=4)** So what can you do in this brave new world of data that affects everything we do?

### 2. 1. What Is Data Science?

#### Supply and demand for data science
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/supply-and-demand-for-data-science?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/supply-and-demand-for-data-science?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] Once upon a time, way back in 2012, which was practically the prehistoric era as far as the data world's concerned.
>
> **[0:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/supply-and-demand-for-data-science?u=76281980&t=8)** I mean, it was before machine learning was common vocabulary.
>
> **[0:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/supply-and-demand-for-data-science?u=76281980&t=11)** It was before deep learning entered the collective unconscious.
>
> **[0:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/supply-and-demand-for-data-science?u=76281980&t=15)** And it was a full ten years before the AI revolution that took over the world.
>
> **[0:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/supply-and-demand-for-data-science?u=76281980&t=20)** Back in 2012, Thomas Davenport and DJ Patil published an article in "Harvard Business Review," in which they famously claimed that data science of all things was, quote, "The sexiest job of the 21st century."
>
> **[0:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/supply-and-demand-for-data-science?u=76281980&t=36)** Now, that's a bold claim.
>
> **[0:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/supply-and-demand-for-data-science?u=76281980&t=38)** The reason for their bold claim was that as they saw it, data scientists one, had a valuable combination of rare qualities that two, put them in high demand.
>
> **[0:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/supply-and-demand-for-data-science?u=76281980&t=51)** Now, this was true in 2012 and is true now, especially if you consider all the other fields that are derived from data science.
>
> **[1:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/supply-and-demand-for-data-science?u=76281980&t=60)** So let's take a closer look at these two elements that they identified, in particular, the rare qualities and the high demand.
>
> **[1:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/supply-and-demand-for-data-science?u=76281980&t=71)** First, the rare qualities.
>
> **[1:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/supply-and-demand-for-data-science?u=76281980&t=73)** Data science enables people to find order, meaning, and value in unstructured data.
>
> **[1:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/supply-and-demand-for-data-science?u=76281980&t=79)** Unstructured data is enormously difficult to work with, and that's been one of the best examples of the power of data science.
>
> **[1:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/supply-and-demand-for-data-science?u=76281980&t=88)** They can then use that data to predict outcomes.
>
> **[1:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/supply-and-demand-for-data-science?u=76281980&t=92)** So who's likely to purchase something, who's likely to pose a security threat, who's likely to develop a disease or respond well to a new treatment?
>
> **[1:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/supply-and-demand-for-data-science?u=76281980&t=100)** All of these are important.
>
> **[1:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/supply-and-demand-for-data-science?u=76281980&t=102)** And they can automate processes, they can give individualized recommendations while people are shopping online, they can identify your friends in photographs, they can give psychological support through AI chatbots.
>
> **[1:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/supply-and-demand-for-data-science?u=76281980&t=114)** And in the process, they developed a whole new paradigm for collaborating with technology, the ways that we engage with technology and our data to answer the questions that are important to us.
>
> **[2:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/supply-and-demand-for-data-science?u=76281980&t=128)** Now that in turn, led to high demand.
>
> **[2:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/supply-and-demand-for-data-science?u=76281980&t=130)** And data science provides hidden insight or insights into data that's not otherwise accessible.
>
> **[2:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/supply-and-demand-for-data-science?u=76281980&t=137)** You couldn't otherwise get that little glimmer that you needed out of the data.
>
> **[2:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/supply-and-demand-for-data-science?u=76281980&t=142)** And that, of course, provides competitive advantage, which is of huge concern to a very large number of organizations.
>
> **[2:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/supply-and-demand-for-data-science?u=76281980&t=150)** And not surprisingly, that created entire new markets and demands that no one even anticipated existing when data science first came along.
>
> **[2:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/supply-and-demand-for-data-science?u=76281980&t=161)** So you want to talk about the global demand.
>
> **[2:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/supply-and-demand-for-data-science?u=76281980&t=163)** Well, there is enormous demand in the US, the UK, Germany, Canada, Australia, France, New Zealand, Singapore, Sweden, Ireland, and these are just the top ten.
>
> **[2:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/supply-and-demand-for-data-science?u=76281980&t=176)** I mean, really everywhere in the world.
>
> **[2:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/supply-and-demand-for-data-science?u=76281980&t=179)** And then looking at the growth in industries.
>
> **[3:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/supply-and-demand-for-data-science?u=76281980&t=182)** Now, you tend to think of just tech companies, but there's a lot more than that.
>
> **[3:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/supply-and-demand-for-data-science?u=76281980&t=188)** Some of the best jobs in data science are in the banking and finance industries, and in healthcare, and medicine, but also the automotive industry, media and entertainment, cybersecurity and retail.
>
> **[3:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/supply-and-demand-for-data-science?u=76281980&t=200)** All of these have had enormous growth for data science-specific skill sets applied in those domains.
>
> **[3:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/supply-and-demand-for-data-science?u=76281980&t=208)** And then third is how do you meet this demand?
>
> **[3:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/supply-and-demand-for-data-science?u=76281980&t=211)** Well, you know, that many years ago there weren't even any academic programs in data science.
>
> **[3:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/supply-and-demand-for-data-science?u=76281980&t=217)** There are now, but a lot of people already have their jobs and consequently, a major emphasis has been on training and development and career switching for people who are already working for the company.
>
> **[3:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/supply-and-demand-for-data-science?u=76281980&t=231)** They're already working for the bank, they're already working for the hospital, and they can add the data science skillset.
>
> **[3:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/supply-and-demand-for-data-science?u=76281980&t=237)** Also, things like remote work, which we all learned about during the pandemic, and no-code solutions.
>
> **[4:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/supply-and-demand-for-data-science?u=76281980&t=243)** So a lot of data science has relied on programming languages, but there are many other applications and ways of working with data that don't require you to write lines of code.
>
> **[4:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/supply-and-demand-for-data-science?u=76281980&t=253)** And we'll talk about some of those later in this course.
>
> **[4:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/supply-and-demand-for-data-science?u=76281980&t=257)** Now there's another thing about salary.
>
> **[4:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/supply-and-demand-for-data-science?u=76281980&t=259)** Data science pays well.
>
> **[4:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/supply-and-demand-for-data-science?u=76281980&t=261)** Here in the United States as of 2024, the job site Glassdoor says that data scientists have a median income of $163,000 a year, which is more than twice, actually, it's 2.6 times the median personal income of $63,000 that they report for all full-time working adults.
>
> **[4:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/supply-and-demand-for-data-science?u=76281980&t=279)** And by the way, that $163,000 is just the industry average.
>
> **[4:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/supply-and-demand-for-data-science?u=76281980&t=283)** Some employers, like the major tech companies, have median salaries that are almost twice that.
>
> **[4:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/supply-and-demand-for-data-science?u=76281980&t=290)** And then people tend to really like these jobs.
>
> **[4:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/supply-and-demand-for-data-science?u=76281980&t=294)** Forbes put computer and mathematical, which specifically includes data science as the number two job category on their list of top ten in-demand, high-paying industries in 2024 from research.
>
> **[5:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/supply-and-demand-for-data-science?u=76281980&t=307)** Also, U.S. News & World Report puts data scientists in their top ten best jobs, along with several other data and tech-adjacent jobs.
>
> **[5:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/supply-and-demand-for-data-science?u=76281980&t=316)** All of this is to say that there's still an enormous demand, there's still enormous potential and still enormous reward for careers and for skills in data science.

#### The data science Venn diagram revisited
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/the-data-science-venn-diagram-revisited?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/the-data-science-venn-diagram-revisited?u=76281980&t=1)** - [Instructor] Sometimes, the whole is greater than the sum of its parts, and you can see this in a lot of different places.
>
> **[0:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/the-data-science-venn-diagram-revisited?u=76281980&t=7)** Take for instance, music.
>
> **[0:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/the-data-science-venn-diagram-revisited?u=76281980&t=8)** You take John, and Paul, and George, and Ringo, all wonderful musicians in their own rights.
>
> **[0:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/the-data-science-venn-diagram-revisited?u=76281980&t=14)** But put them together, and you have The Beatles and you have revolutionized popular culture.
>
> **[0:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/the-data-science-venn-diagram-revisited?u=76281980&t=21)** Or take the fact that everybody has a circle of friends, and basically everybody has the internet now, and you have created social networks and you have revolutionized the computing world.
>
> **[0:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/the-data-science-venn-diagram-revisited?u=76281980&t=33)** Or in 2013, Drew Conway proposed the combination of hacking skills, that's computer programming, and math and statistics, and substantive or topical domain expertise, together give you data science, a new field that has revolutionized both the technology and the business world.
>
> **[0:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/the-data-science-venn-diagram-revisited?u=76281980&t=53)** And I want to talk a little more about why each of those three elements in the Venn diagram of data science are so important.
>
> **[1:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/the-data-science-venn-diagram-revisited?u=76281980&t=60)** First one, the hacking skills or computer programming.
>
> **[1:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/the-data-science-venn-diagram-revisited?u=76281980&t=63)** The reason that's important is because you have such novel sources of data.
>
> **[1:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/the-data-science-venn-diagram-revisited?u=76281980&t=67)** You have social media and social networks.
>
> **[1:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/the-data-science-venn-diagram-revisited?u=76281980&t=69)** You have challenging formats, like the graph data from those social networks, or images, or video that don't fit into the rows and columns of a spreadsheet.
>
> **[1:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/the-data-science-venn-diagram-revisited?u=76281980&t=78)** Or you have streaming data, like sensor data or live web data, that comes in so fast that you can't pause it to analyze it.
>
> **[1:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/the-data-science-venn-diagram-revisited?u=76281980&t=86)** All of these require the creativity that comes with hacking and the ability to work freely with what you have in front of you.
>
> **[1:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/the-data-science-venn-diagram-revisited?u=76281980&t=96)** Now, in terms of actual computer programming skills, there's a few things that are very useful in data science.
>
> **[1:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/the-data-science-venn-diagram-revisited?u=76281980&t=102)** The ability to work with a language like Python or R.
>
> **[1:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/the-data-science-venn-diagram-revisited?u=76281980&t=105)** These are programming languages that are very frequently used for data manipulation and modeling.
>
> **[1:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/the-data-science-venn-diagram-revisited?u=76281980&t=111)** There's C, and C++, and Java.
>
> **[1:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/the-data-science-venn-diagram-revisited?u=76281980&t=114)** These are general-purpose languages that are used for the backend, the foundational elements of data science, and they provide maximum speed.
>
> **[2:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/the-data-science-venn-diagram-revisited?u=76281980&t=122)** There's SQL, or SQL.
>
> **[2:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/the-data-science-venn-diagram-revisited?u=76281980&t=124)** That stands for structured query language.
>
> **[2:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/the-data-science-venn-diagram-revisited?u=76281980&t=126)** This is the language for working with relational databases to do queries and data manipulation.
>
> **[2:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/the-data-science-venn-diagram-revisited?u=76281980&t=133)** And then there are packages you can use in other languages, like TensorFlow.
>
> **[2:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/the-data-science-venn-diagram-revisited?u=76281980&t=137)** This is an open source library that's used for deep learning that has revolutionized the way that data science is performed right now.
>
> **[2:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/the-data-science-venn-diagram-revisited?u=76281980&t=147)** And then there's the mathematical elements of data science.
>
> **[2:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/the-data-science-venn-diagram-revisited?u=76281980&t=150)** First off, there are several forms of mathematics that are particularly useful in data science.
>
> **[2:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/the-data-science-venn-diagram-revisited?u=76281980&t=155)** There's probability, and linear algebra, and calculus, and regression, and I'll talk about some of each of these.
>
> **[2:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/the-data-science-venn-diagram-revisited?u=76281980&t=162)** But they allow you to do something important.
>
> **[2:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/the-data-science-venn-diagram-revisited?u=76281980&t=164)** Number one, they allow you to choose the procedures.
>
> **[2:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/the-data-science-venn-diagram-revisited?u=76281980&t=167)** You want to judge the fit between your question, which is always the first and most important thing; the data that you have available to you; and then you choose a procedure that answers your questions based on your data.
>
> **[2:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/the-data-science-venn-diagram-revisited?u=76281980&t=179)** And if you understand the mathematics and how it works, you'll be able to make a much better and more informed choice.
>
> **[3:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/the-data-science-venn-diagram-revisited?u=76281980&t=187)** And also, you'll be able to diagnose problems.
>
> **[3:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/the-data-science-venn-diagram-revisited?u=76281980&t=190)** Murphy's law applies in data science, as well as everywhere else that anything that can go wrong will go wrong, and you need to know what to do when the procedures that you chosen fail or they give sometimes impossible results.
>
> **[3:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/the-data-science-venn-diagram-revisited?u=76281980&t=202)** You need to understand exactly how the data's being manipulated so you can see where the trouble areas are and how to resolve them.
>
> **[3:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/the-data-science-venn-diagram-revisited?u=76281980&t=211)** And then the third area of Conway's data science Venn Diagram is substantive expertise.
>
> **[3:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/the-data-science-venn-diagram-revisited?u=76281980&t=217)** This is each domain or topic area has its own goals, methods, and constraints.
>
> **[3:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/the-data-science-venn-diagram-revisited?u=76281980&t=223)** If you're working in social media marketing, you're going to have a very different set of goals and methods than if you're working in biomedical informatics.
>
> **[3:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/the-data-science-venn-diagram-revisited?u=76281980&t=232)** And you need to know what constitutes value in the particular domain you're working in.
>
> **[3:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/the-data-science-venn-diagram-revisited?u=76281980&t=238)** And finally, how to implement the insights, because data science is an action-oriented field.
>
> **[4:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/the-data-science-venn-diagram-revisited?u=76281980&t=244)** It's designed to tell you what to do next, to get the most value, provide the best service that you possibly can based on the data that you have.
>
> **[4:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/the-data-science-venn-diagram-revisited?u=76281980&t=253)** And it's important to know that the data science Venn diagram, proposed in 2013 over 10 years ago, is not really static.
>
> **[4:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/the-data-science-venn-diagram-revisited?u=76281980&t=262)** People have proposed other important facets or potential circles to add to it that give data science even greater value than before.
>
> **[4:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/the-data-science-venn-diagram-revisited?u=76281980&t=272)** So it's not just the code, quant, and context, or the hacking the mass stats, and the domain expertise.
>
> **[4:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/the-data-science-venn-diagram-revisited?u=76281980&t=279)** Other important skills include communication, the ability to understand exactly what it is your stakeholders are asking for, and to communicate the results effectively to them and to work well with your team.
>
> **[4:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/the-data-science-venn-diagram-revisited?u=76281980&t=291)** Decision-making is a separate thing.
>
> **[4:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/the-data-science-venn-diagram-revisited?u=76281980&t=295)** When you do your analysis, ideally, you would end with specific actionable insights that can be carried out by your stakeholder.
>
> **[5:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/the-data-science-venn-diagram-revisited?u=76281980&t=304)** That means that you need to be comfortable making a decision and telling them what the single best plan of action is.
>
> **[5:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/the-data-science-venn-diagram-revisited?u=76281980&t=312)** And then always and forever, ethics constitute an important separate skill that overrides every element of data science, understanding the impact of gathering your data and processing it, and the effects that your decisions can have on other people.
>
> **[5:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/the-data-science-venn-diagram-revisited?u=76281980&t=328)** If you do those throughout, if you incorporate them, you will be able to have a greater impact that has a greater lasting productive impact.
>
> **[5:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/the-data-science-venn-diagram-revisited?u=76281980&t=337)** And so taken together with the three original facets of the data science Venn diagram, these three additional facets, communication, decision-making, and ethics, can give you added value not just into your data work in general, but the entire productivity of the organizations that you're working with.

#### The CRISP-DM framework
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/the-crisp-dm-framework?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/the-crisp-dm-framework?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] So, it turns out that I am not necessarily the most organized person in the world.
>
> **[0:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/the-crisp-dm-framework?u=76281980&t=6)** I have, in fact, had times that important documents and even data were stored approximately like this.
>
> **[0:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/the-crisp-dm-framework?u=76281980&t=14)** But we all know that the composting approach to organization makes your data projects a lot harder, which is why some very smart people have spent a lot of time thinking about how to better organize data projects more effectively.
>
> **[0:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/the-crisp-dm-framework?u=76281980&t=33)** And one of the most common approaches in the data mining world is something called CRISP-DM, which is short for cross-industry standard process for data mining.
>
> **[0:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/the-crisp-dm-framework?u=76281980&t=48)** So, this is a great way of thinking about how to organize data projects, not just in data mining, but really anywhere.
>
> **[0:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/the-crisp-dm-framework?u=76281980&t=56)** And CRISP-DM describes a data project as having six phases.
>
> **[1:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/the-crisp-dm-framework?u=76281980&t=62)** Now, again, they're specifically talking about data mining, but you can apply it to anything.
>
> **[1:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/the-crisp-dm-framework?u=76281980&t=66)** So, the first phase is business understanding, and the idea here is, what's the business objective?
>
> **[1:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/the-crisp-dm-framework?u=76281980&t=73)** What is your actual goal?
>
> **[1:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/the-crisp-dm-framework?u=76281980&t=75)** And then the situation assessment and determine the data mining goal.
>
> **[1:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/the-crisp-dm-framework?u=76281980&t=79)** Again, trying to know what you're trying to accomplish as you go through the project and then to produce a project plan, actually write down, create the map so you know when you're at the goal.
>
> **[1:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/the-crisp-dm-framework?u=76281980&t=92)** The next step is the data understanding.
>
> **[1:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/the-crisp-dm-framework?u=76281980&t=95)** So, you collect the initial data, you describe the data, you explore it, you verify the data quality, an important step that if you don't perform adequately, everything else can go straight out the window as you're going.
>
> **[1:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/the-crisp-dm-framework?u=76281980&t=110)** And then you have data preparation.
>
> **[1:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/the-crisp-dm-framework?u=76281980&t=113)** So, you get your data set and you select data and you clean the data and you construct the data by, for instance, creating indicators or factor scores or features that you're going to be using to build your models.
>
> **[2:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/the-crisp-dm-framework?u=76281980&t=129)** You can also integrate the data with not just this current dataset, but with other data sets that are available to you to bring in extra meaning, and then formatting the data in an appropriate way for the tools and the analysis that you're going to conduct.
>
> **[2:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/the-crisp-dm-framework?u=76281980&t=144)** After that is modeling, where you select a modeling technique, you generate a test design, you build the model, so, for instance, you do your neural network, you do your random forest, you assess the model.
>
> **[2:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/the-crisp-dm-framework?u=76281980&t=158)** Often if you're doing a classification task, that looks at how accurate is it or what is the level of specificity or sensitivity to certain conditions, then you have evaluation.
>
> **[2:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/the-crisp-dm-framework?u=76281980&t=170)** So, you evaluate the results and you review the process.
>
> **[2:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/the-crisp-dm-framework?u=76281980&t=174)** How well did this go over?
>
> **[2:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/the-crisp-dm-framework?u=76281980&t=176)** And then you determine the next steps.
>
> **[2:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/the-crisp-dm-framework?u=76281980&t=179)** And then you finish in CRISP-DM with deployment.
>
> **[3:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/the-crisp-dm-framework?u=76281980&t=184)** I like to think it's the we're open for business stage.
>
> **[3:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/the-crisp-dm-framework?u=76281980&t=187)** You plan the deployment, what you're actually going to do with your results, as well as plan the monitoring and maintenance.
>
> **[3:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/the-crisp-dm-framework?u=76281980&t=194)** Because what you find is there is often drift between a model established at one point in time and the way the data evolves.
>
> **[3:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/the-crisp-dm-framework?u=76281980&t=203)** And so, you need to check up on it frequently.
>
> **[3:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/the-crisp-dm-framework?u=76281980&t=205)** And then there's producing a final report to the stakeholders and then reviewing the project overall.
>
> **[3:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/the-crisp-dm-framework?u=76281980&t=212)** Taken together, these steps can be one very helpful way and one well-established way in certain fields for planning and organizing a data project to make sure you cover all your bases, you check the list, make sure you're getting done what you need to, and that gives you the best chance of having efficiency the first time through to get the value from the data and send that off to your stakeholders.
>
> **[4:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/the-crisp-dm-framework?u=76281980&t=241)** Now, even though this is a very common approach, it is worth mentioning that there has been some developmental work and there has been an evolution of this approach.
>
> **[4:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/the-crisp-dm-framework?u=76281980&t=250)** One interesting variation that gives you more choices, always more than one way to go, was proposed in 1950, excuse me, is known as ASUM or ASUM-DM, which stands for analytics solution unified method for data mining.
>
> **[4:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/the-crisp-dm-framework?u=76281980&t=267)** Again, of course, that was proposed by IBM in 2015 as an enhancement of CRISP-DM.
>
> **[4:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/the-crisp-dm-framework?u=76281980&t=273)** And what it does is it adds some new features or new elements to the planning approach.
>
> **[4:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/the-crisp-dm-framework?u=76281980&t=279)** It includes addressing infrastructure, specifically project management, deployment, documentation, and workflow detail.
>
> **[4:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/the-crisp-dm-framework?u=76281980&t=285)** And most importantly, for a lot of people, it specifically incorporates elements of agile methodology, that's going to make it fit really well within the project management framework that's adopted by a lot of major organizations.
>
> **[5:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/the-crisp-dm-framework?u=76281980&t=301)** But whichever method you use, the best thing that you can do is make a plan for your project, get everybody on the same page, and use it so you can work effectively and efficiently and reach the goals of actionable insights and impact for your project.

#### Roles, teams, and tools in modern data science
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/roles-teams-and-tools-in-modern-data-science?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/roles-teams-and-tools-in-modern-data-science?u=76281980&t=1)** - [Instructor] Data science is fundamentally a team sport.
>
> **[0:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/roles-teams-and-tools-in-modern-data-science?u=76281980&t=4)** There are so many different skills and so many different elements involved in a data science project that you're going to need people from all sorts of different backgrounds and with different techniques to contribute to the overall success of the project.
>
> **[0:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/roles-teams-and-tools-in-modern-data-science?u=76281980&t=18)** I want to talk about a few of these important roles.

> **[0:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/roles-teams-and-tools-in-modern-data-science?u=76281980&t=25)** These are the developers and the system architects, the people who focus on the hardware and the software that make data science possible.
>
> **[0:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/roles-teams-and-tools-in-modern-data-science?u=76281980&t=33)** They provide the foundation for all of the other analyses.
>

>
> **[0:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/roles-teams-and-tools-in-modern-data-science?u=76281980&t=44)** Next are machine learning specialists.

> **[0:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/roles-teams-and-tools-in-modern-data-science?u=76281980&t=51)** They work in deep learning, they work in artificial intelligence, and they're the ones who have the intimate understanding of the algorithms and understand exactly how they're working with the data to produce the results that you're looking for.
>
> **[1:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/roles-teams-and-tools-in-modern-data-science?u=76281980&t=66)** In an entirely different vein are people who are researchers, and by that I mean topical researchers.

>
> **[1:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/roles-teams-and-tools-in-modern-data-science?u=76281980&t=82)** And these kinds of researchers, while they connect with data science, they are usually better versed in the design of research within their particular field and doing common statistical analysis.
>
> **[1:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/roles-teams-and-tools-in-modern-data-science?u=76281980&t=94)** That's where their expertise lies, but they connect with data science in that they're trying to find the answers to some of these big picture questions that data scientists can also contribute to.

> **[2:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/roles-teams-and-tools-in-modern-data-science?u=76281980&t=126)** These allow people to make decisions.
>
> **[2:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/roles-teams-and-tools-in-modern-data-science?u=76281980&t=129)** It's for good business decision-making that lets you see how you're performing, where you need to reorient, and how you can better reach your goals.

>
> **[2:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/roles-teams-and-tools-in-modern-data-science?u=76281980&t=147)** And they're in charge of doing a couple of very important things.
>
> **[2:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/roles-teams-and-tools-in-modern-data-science?u=76281980&t=150)** One is they need to frame the business-relevant questions and solutions, so they're the ones who have the big picture.
>
> **[2:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/roles-teams-and-tools-in-modern-data-science?u=76281980&t=155)** They know what they're trying to accomplish with that, and then they need to keep people on track and moving towards it.

> **[2:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/roles-teams-and-tools-in-modern-data-science?u=76281980&t=161)** And to do that, they don't necessarily need to know how to do a neural network, they don't need to make the data visualization, but they need to speak data so they can understand how the data relates to the question they're trying to answer, and they can help take the information that the other people are getting and putting it together into a cohesive whole.
>
> **[3:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/roles-teams-and-tools-in-modern-data-science?u=76281980&t=182)** Now, there are people who are entrepreneurs, and in this case you might have a data-based startup.

> **[3:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/roles-teams-and-tools-in-modern-data-science?u=76281980&t=196)** You also need some great creativity in planning your projects and the execution that get you towards your entrepreneurial goals.
>
> **[3:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/roles-teams-and-tools-in-modern-data-science?u=76281980&t=205)** And then there's the unicorn, also known as the rockstar or the ninja.
>
> **[3:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/roles-teams-and-tools-in-modern-data-science?u=76281980&t=210)** This is a full stack data scientist who can do it all and do it at absolute peak performance.
>
> **[3:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/roles-teams-and-tools-in-modern-data-science?u=76281980&t=217)** Well, it's a nice thing to have.
>
> **[3:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/roles-teams-and-tools-in-modern-data-science?u=76281980&t=219)** On the other hand, that thing is very rare, which is why we call them the unicorn.
>
> **[3:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/roles-teams-and-tools-in-modern-data-science?u=76281980&t=222)** Also, you don't want to rely on one person for everything, aside from the fact that they're hard to find and sometimes hard to keep, you're only getting a single perspective or approach to your business questions, and you usually need something more diverse than that.
>
> **[3:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/roles-teams-and-tools-in-modern-data-science?u=76281980&t=237)** And what that suggests is the common approach to getting all the skills you need for a data project, and that is by team.
>
> **[4:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/roles-teams-and-tools-in-modern-data-science?u=76281980&t=245)** And you can get a unicorn by team, where you can get the people who have all the necessary skills, from the foundational data engineers to the machine learning specialists, to the analysts, to the managers, all working together to get the insight from your data and help your project reach its greatest potential in moving your organization towards its own goals.

#### The central role of questions in data science
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/the-central-role-of-questions-in-data-science?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/the-central-role-of-questions-in-data-science?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] You as a data scientist are in the business of answering questions.
>
> **[0:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/the-central-role-of-questions-in-data-science?u=76281980&t=5)** A person, say the marketing director, comes to you with some kind of question.
>
> **[0:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/the-central-role-of-questions-in-data-science?u=76281980&t=9)** So you gather and you process and analyze the data.
>
> **[0:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/the-central-role-of-questions-in-data-science?u=76281980&t=13)** You build a model or several models, and you come up with an answer to the question that motivated the project.
>
> **[0:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/the-central-role-of-questions-in-data-science?u=76281980&t=20)** But chances are, if you've been at this for a while, it's a question that you've been asked before, and the answer you've given is closely related to the answers that you have also given before.
>
> **[0:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/the-central-role-of-questions-in-data-science?u=76281980&t=34)** But one of the strange things about life, including data science, is that the real value isn't always in the answers.
>
> **[0:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/the-central-role-of-questions-in-data-science?u=76281980&t=42)** For example, here's something from Esther Dyson, a forward-looking investor and philanthropist.
>
> **[0:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/the-central-role-of-questions-in-data-science?u=76281980&t=48)** She says, "The definition of the problem rather than its solution will be the scarce resource in the future."
>
> **[0:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/the-central-role-of-questions-in-data-science?u=76281980&t=55)** Think about that.
>
> **[0:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/the-central-role-of-questions-in-data-science?u=76281980&t=57)** She is saying that answers or solutions will be less valuable than the actual questions that motivate them.
>
> **[1:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/the-central-role-of-questions-in-data-science?u=76281980&t=66)** And I think that's true in data science.
>
> **[1:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/the-central-role-of-questions-in-data-science?u=76281980&t=70)** So you need to change your perspective and find a new way to ask questions that can be answered with your approaches.
>
> **[1:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/the-central-role-of-questions-in-data-science?u=76281980&t=79)** Look at the problem differently and see what extra value you can bring in.
>
> **[1:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/the-central-role-of-questions-in-data-science?u=76281980&t=86)** So it might be helpful, for instance, to think of the tools that you use.
>
> **[1:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/the-central-role-of-questions-in-data-science?u=76281980&t=90)** If you think of some of the most common tools used when working with data, things that you've probably used hundreds or even thousands of times, things like T-tests, regression, classification, principal component analysis, probability values among lots of others.
>
> **[1:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/the-central-role-of-questions-in-data-science?u=76281980&t=107)** The big question here is what exactly do these procedures do compared to how are they interpreted?
>
> **[1:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/the-central-role-of-questions-in-data-science?u=76281980&t=114)** So for example, a T-test is used to compare the means of two groups, and that's the bread and butter of AB testing in the user design world.
>
> **[2:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/the-central-role-of-questions-in-data-science?u=76281980&t=125)** Well, T-test make some assumptions first off.
>
> **[2:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/the-central-role-of-questions-in-data-science?u=76281980&t=128)** They only work properly when you have normal distributions, that's bell curves, and that you have similar sample sizes in your two groups, and you have approximately equal variance.
>
> **[2:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/the-central-role-of-questions-in-data-science?u=76281980&t=139)** You also have independent observations.
>
> **[2:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/the-central-role-of-questions-in-data-science?u=76281980&t=142)** They're kind of sensitive to these things, and what they tell you is whether the means of those two groups are different.
>
> **[2:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/the-central-role-of-questions-in-data-science?u=76281980&t=150)** What's important there is they ignore other differences.
>
> **[2:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/the-central-role-of-questions-in-data-science?u=76281980&t=153)** If the median were different, doesn't care if there's outliers on one or the other, doesn't care if there's a spread in variance, it doesn't look at that.
>
> **[2:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/the-central-role-of-questions-in-data-science?u=76281980&t=162)** And so people often use the T-test to indicate whether two groups are the same or different.
>
> **[2:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/the-central-role-of-questions-in-data-science?u=76281980&t=167)** But remember, it only looks at one point, the mean of each groups.
>
> **[2:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/the-central-role-of-questions-in-data-science?u=76281980&t=172)** And so if you're trying to think a little more creatively, you might want to look beyond just that one element of that one test as a way of trying to bring some extra value into your work.
>
> **[3:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/the-central-role-of-questions-in-data-science?u=76281980&t=186)** In fact, when you start thinking a little more creatively about the questions that you could answer and the methods that you could use to explore them, then you find that your data science can get a lot more compelling.
>
> **[3:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/the-central-role-of-questions-in-data-science?u=76281980&t=200)** So think about it, the reports are going to be more interesting.
>
> **[3:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/the-central-role-of-questions-in-data-science?u=76281980&t=204)** You're not telling people the same stuff they've had before.
>
> **[3:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/the-central-role-of-questions-in-data-science?u=76281980&t=207)** I understand the value of predictability in dashboards, which are very useful for getting a idea of a constant process.
>
> **[3:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/the-central-role-of-questions-in-data-science?u=76281980&t=217)** But again, data science, you're usually being asked to do something novel.
>
> **[3:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/the-central-role-of-questions-in-data-science?u=76281980&t=220)** And so you can get more interesting insights.
>
> **[3:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/the-central-role-of-questions-in-data-science?u=76281980&t=224)** Also, by using these different approaches and thinking maybe this common approach isn't what I need, you can find some hidden value.
>
> **[3:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/the-central-role-of-questions-in-data-science?u=76281980&t=232)** And again, that's one of the things that makes data science so important is the ability to get to that hidden value.
>
> **[4:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/the-central-role-of-questions-in-data-science?u=76281980&t=241)** And obviously, by extension, that also tells you that you can get some competitive advantage for the people who've commissioned this project.
>
> **[4:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/the-central-role-of-questions-in-data-science?u=76281980&t=249)** Again, by finding something unexpected in there, by using a creative approach, you can present it to them in a way that both gets their attention and helps them further their business.
>
> **[4:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/the-central-role-of-questions-in-data-science?u=76281980&t=260)** And that is the great advantage of data science and thinking about new questions.
>
> **[4:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/the-central-role-of-questions-in-data-science?u=76281980&t=265)** So you don't want to just find answers.
>
> **[4:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/the-central-role-of-questions-in-data-science?u=76281980&t=269)** That's maybe what they pay you for, what they are expecting, but you can do more than that.
>
> **[4:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/the-central-role-of-questions-in-data-science?u=76281980&t=277)** By learning to ask better, more interesting and more informative questions and getting the answers to them, you can find value and that is where the promise of data science is realized.

> [!info]- Semantic Content
>
> **CLI Commands:** find (5), make (1)
> **Analogies:** for example (2), for instance (1)
> **Code Keywords:** while, (1), for, (1)

### 3. 2. The Place of Data Science in the Data Universe

#### Artificial intelligence
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/artificial-intelligence?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/artificial-intelligence?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Lecturer] The human mind seems to work in mysterious ways, and sometimes conceptually and empirically distinct phenomena seem to occupy the same cognitive space, and as a result can get muddled up in the process.
>
> **[0:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/artificial-intelligence?u=76281980&t=15)** That seems to be the case for data science and for artificial intelligence, which are sometimes treated as synonyms.
>
> **[0:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/artificial-intelligence?u=76281980&t=22)** But before I compare and contrast the two fields, 'cause there are differences, I want to mention a few things about the nature of categories and definitions.
>
> **[0:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/artificial-intelligence?u=76281980&t=33)** The first thing is that categories are constructs.
>
> **[0:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/artificial-intelligence?u=76281980&t=36)** They're not things that exist out there in the world, but they are ways of thinking about things.
>
> **[0:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/artificial-intelligence?u=76281980&t=43)** So, they're constructed mental cognitive phenomena.
>
> **[0:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/artificial-intelligence?u=76281980&t=48)** You put them together, which means they can be put together in different ways.
>

>
> **[0:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/artificial-intelligence?u=76281980&t=59)** They don't exist for their own personal satisfaction.
>
> **[1:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/artificial-intelligence?u=76281980&t=63)** Somebody created them because they allowed them to accomplish a particular task.
>
> **[1:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/artificial-intelligence?u=76281980&t=69)** And the final thing is that the use of constructs varies by need.
>
> **[1:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/artificial-intelligence?u=76281980&t=75)** The idea here is that maybe your constructs need to change, be reframed depending on what you're doing at the moment 'cause there's not an inherent inescapable truth to them.
>
> **[1:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/artificial-intelligence?u=76281980&t=88)** But again, they are conveniences, they are manners of speaking.

> **[1:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/artificial-intelligence?u=76281980&t=92)** And this whole thing about constructs and definitions, it makes me think about the question of whether tomatoes are fruits or vegetables.
>
> **[1:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/artificial-intelligence?u=76281980&t=99)** Now, everybody knows that tomatoes are supposed to be fruit, but everybody also knows that you would never put tomatoes in a fruit salad.
>
> **[1:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/artificial-intelligence?u=76281980&t=107)** Instead, they go on a vegetable plate with the carrots and celery.
>
> **[1:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/artificial-intelligence?u=76281980&t=111)** Now, the answer to this paradox is actually simple.
>
> **[1:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/artificial-intelligence?u=76281980&t=115)** Fruit is a botanical term.
>
> **[1:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/artificial-intelligence?u=76281980&t=117)** Vegetable is a culinary term.
>
> **[2:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/artificial-intelligence?u=76281980&t=120)** They're not parallel or even very well coordinated systems of categorization, which is why confusion like this can arise.
>
> **[2:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/artificial-intelligence?u=76281980&t=129)** Also, anybody who's ever tried to organize their music or their movies knows that categories are shifty things.
>
> **[2:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/artificial-intelligence?u=76281980&t=136)** There are dozens, hundreds of categories of hip hop music, as well as opera, heavy metal, or what have you.
>
> **[2:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/artificial-intelligence?u=76281980&t=143)** Long ago I decided that instead of trying to identify some sort of intrinsic essence, the true category of the music, it was best to simply give categories for things that I wanted to hear together, regardless of how other people thought of them, or even what the artist thought.
>
> **[2:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/artificial-intelligence?u=76281980&t=159)** It was a functional category for me.
>
> **[2:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/artificial-intelligence?u=76281980&t=163)** And that gets us back to the question of data science and artificial intelligence.
>
> **[2:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/artificial-intelligence?u=76281980&t=168)** These are functional categories.
>
> **[2:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/artificial-intelligence?u=76281980&t=170)** And so let's go back to what do we even mean by artificial intelligence?
>
> **[2:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/artificial-intelligence?u=76281980&t=175)** Well, there's a joke that it simply means whatever thing a computer can't do, that's intelligence.
>
> **[3:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/artificial-intelligence?u=76281980&t=182)** Well, obviously that's a joke because computers are always learning how to do new things.
>
> **[3:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/artificial-intelligence?u=76281980&t=187)** People set a standard, the computer achieves it, and they say, "Well, that's not really intelligence, it's something else."
>
> **[3:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/artificial-intelligence?u=76281980&t=192)** Another way to think about it is artificial intelligence is when computers are able to accomplish tasks that normally require humans to do them.
>
> **[3:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/artificial-intelligence?u=76281980&t=202)** Now, what's interesting about that is these two elements, whatever a computer can't do and tests that require humans, those definitions really kind of go back to the '50s at the first major boom of artificial intelligence, when researchers were trying many different approaches to have computers do the work of humans.
>
> **[3:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/artificial-intelligence?u=76281980&t=222)** Many of those approaches were based on extensive coding of expert knowledge and decision paths, think of enormous decision trees, that more recently became known as Good Old-Fashioned Artificial Intelligence, or G-O-F-A-I or GOFAI.
>
> **[3:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/artificial-intelligence?u=76281980&t=239)** The approach was promising for a little while, but it ultimately faded when the magnitude of the task became apparent, and also realizing that the work that they had done didn't have the flexibility needed for what the researchers were hoping for, which is some sort of true general intelligence.
>
> **[4:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/artificial-intelligence?u=76281980&t=258)** And so more recently, artificial intelligence has come to refer to programs, or algorithms, or sequences of equations, or computer code that can learn from the data.
>
> **[4:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/artificial-intelligence?u=76281980&t=272)** Now, some of these are very simple approaches and some of them are extraordinarily sophisticated, but they allow the computers to do things that, again, normally humans would've done, and the computers can get better and better at it.
>
> **[4:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/artificial-intelligence?u=76281980&t=285)** Some examples of this include classifying photos without human assistance, translating text, or even spoken language from one language to another, or mastering games like Go or chess, or other games that people thought a machine would never be able to do.
>
> **[5:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/artificial-intelligence?u=76281980&t=303)** And so this last one, that is a program that can learn from data is probably the best working definition of artificial intelligence.
>
> **[5:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/artificial-intelligence?u=76281980&t=313)** And while it can include very simple models, a regression model for example, it usually refers to two approaches in particular, machine learning algorithms as a general category and deep learning neural networks as a particular instance.
>
> **[5:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/artificial-intelligence?u=76281980&t=332)** I'm going to say more about each of those elsewhere, but I did want to bring up one more important distinction when talking about AI.
>
> **[5:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/artificial-intelligence?u=76281980&t=339)** And that is the difference between what is called strong or general AI, where you want to have a replica of the human brain that can solve any task.
>
> **[5:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/artificial-intelligence?u=76281980&t=346)** And that's the thing that we normally think of in science fiction, the computer that can talk to you and intuit all sorts of things.
>
> **[5:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/artificial-intelligence?u=76281980&t=354)** That was the original goal of artificial intelligence research back in the '50s.
>
> **[5:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/artificial-intelligence?u=76281980&t=359)** But it ended up being really unworkable.
>
> **[6:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/artificial-intelligence?u=76281980&t=363)** And instead, when researchers refocused, instead of trying to create a general purpose mechanical brain to what is sometimes called weak or narrow AI, that is algorithms that focus on a specific well-defined task, there was enormous growth.
>
> **[6:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/artificial-intelligence?u=76281980&t=380)** It turned out that this focus, this specificity, is what made the explosive growth of AI possible.
>
> **[6:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/artificial-intelligence?u=76281980&t=388)** But that explosive growth was really here for predictive AI or AI models that were good at replicating the things that humans could do, again, mostly on specific tasks.
>
> **[6:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/artificial-intelligence?u=76281980&t=400)** Things changed dramatically in 2022, specifically ChatGPT was released to the general public on the 30th of November, 2022.
>
> **[6:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/artificial-intelligence?u=76281980&t=410)** And while generative AI had existed before that, this is when it just kind of exploded onto the scene.
>
> **[6:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/artificial-intelligence?u=76281980&t=419)** And that changed a lot of other elements, especially about how AI is interpreted and how it applies to data science in general.
>
> **[7:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/artificial-intelligence?u=76281980&t=427)** So, for instance, again, we have predictive AI that is the machine learning that we became familiar with over the last 10 years, where an algorithm predicts how a human would complete a similar task like is this a dog or is it cat in the video?
>
> **[7:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/artificial-intelligence?u=76281980&t=443)** And that's to be contrasted to generative AI, which creates new information.
>
> **[7:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/artificial-intelligence?u=76281980&t=450)** So, the algorithm isn't just deciding what is this?
>
> **[7:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/artificial-intelligence?u=76281980&t=452)** What is that? Or what does this text mean?
>
> **[7:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/artificial-intelligence?u=76281980&t=455)** It is making new text, it is making a new image, video, audio, et cetera, and that's a fundamentally different approach.
>
> **[7:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/artificial-intelligence?u=76281980&t=464)** Now, this relies on something called transformers and intention mechanisms.
>
> **[7:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/artificial-intelligence?u=76281980&t=469)** The transformers are the foundation of generative AI models like GPT, which stands for Generative Pre-trained Transformer, or BERT, which is for Bi-directional Encoder Representations from Transformers, and other approaches.
>
> **[8:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/artificial-intelligence?u=76281980&t=482)** I'll say more about those in other videos, but this is the extremely basic foundational method that's used for generative AI.
>
> **[8:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/artificial-intelligence?u=76281980&t=493)** And it gets back a little bit to this question I raised originally about fruits versus vegetables.
>
> **[8:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/artificial-intelligence?u=76281980&t=499)** What is AI? What is data science?
>
> **[8:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/artificial-intelligence?u=76281980&t=501)** Well, artificial intelligence, you can think of it as algorithms that learn from many kinds of data to either predict or to create in a human manner.
>
> **[8:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/artificial-intelligence?u=76281980&t=511)** And this is to be contrasted with data science, which is the collection of skills and techniques for dealing with challenging data.
>
> **[8:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/artificial-intelligence?u=76281980&t=520)** And by using these particular definitions, AI nearly always involves data science.
>
> **[8:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/artificial-intelligence?u=76281980&t=527)** Whereas most data science projects do not evolve AI, at least in the form of neural networks for attention based transformers.
>
> **[8:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/artificial-intelligence?u=76281980&t=536)** Let's think a little more about three different elements.
>
> **[8:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/artificial-intelligence?u=76281980&t=539)** We want to talk about data science, which refers to insights from data.
>
> **[9:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/artificial-intelligence?u=76281980&t=543)** You have the data in front of you, you're trying to find something in it.
>
> **[9:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/artificial-intelligence?u=76281980&t=546)** Machine learning, which is data-driven learning algorithms that can learn from the data and artificial intelligence, which is designed to simulate human thinking.
>
> **[9:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/artificial-intelligence?u=76281980&t=556)** Now, I want to show you a rough approximation I created of the overlap and the interplay between these three elements.
>
> **[9:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/artificial-intelligence?u=76281980&t=564)** Here's another data science Venn diagram.
>
> **[9:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/artificial-intelligence?u=76281980&t=567)** We have data science here, we have machine learning here, and we have artificial intelligence AI here.
>
> **[9:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/artificial-intelligence?u=76281980&t=574)** At the connection between data science and machine learning, that might be a good place to put predictive analytics because that is work that was there before the AI, especially the generative AI revolution of using data that you had to work hard to get it ready and machine learning to find the patterns in it to make specific predictions.
>
> **[9:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/artificial-intelligence?u=76281980&t=595)** At the intersection between data science and AI, well, that might be an example of expert systems.
>
> **[10:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/artificial-intelligence?u=76281980&t=600)** And that goes back to the good old fashioned AI dating all the way back to the '50s where you're trying to build a model usually by programming it that is able to approximate humans.
>
> **[10:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/artificial-intelligence?u=76281980&t=613)** This doesn't involve the automated elements of machine learning.
>
> **[10:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/artificial-intelligence?u=76281980&t=617)** And then if we go to AI and machine learning, well, reinforcement learning is one possible example of the interaction between those two without necessarily involving the elements of data science.
>
> **[10:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/artificial-intelligence?u=76281980&t=630)** But take them all together, and that intersection between the three is one way of thinking about the foundation of generative AI.
>
> **[10:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/artificial-intelligence?u=76281980&t=641)** And so while these are distinct domains, they always overlap and they inform each other, and truthfully, they reinforce each other to help data have greater impact in the world and in the organizations that you're working with.
