### 9. 8. Algorithms That Create

#### Generative Adversarial Networks (GANs)
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/generative-adversarial-networks-gans?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/generative-adversarial-networks-gans?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] This painting is called "Edmond de Belamy," and it's notable for a few reasons aside from being pretty smudgy and impressionistic.
>
> **[0:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/generative-adversarial-networks-gans?u=76281980&t=10)** First, it sold in 2018 at auction for over $400,000, and that's a lot of money by most people's standards.
>
> **[0:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/generative-adversarial-networks-gans?u=76281980&t=19)** Second, if you take a closer look at the bottom right of the picture where the artist typically signs their name, you'll see not a name but a mathematical formula.
>
> **[0:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/generative-adversarial-networks-gans?u=76281980&t=30)** In fact, this formula is part of a computer algorithm that produced the painting based on its experience viewing over 15,000 portraits from WikiArt.
>
> **[0:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/generative-adversarial-networks-gans?u=76281980&t=42)** This was an algorithmically produced work of art.
>
> **[0:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/generative-adversarial-networks-gans?u=76281980&t=47)** It was created with what is called a generative adversarial network, and that actually consists of two pieces.
>
> **[0:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/generative-adversarial-networks-gans?u=76281980&t=54)** First, there is a generative network, or a generator.
>
> **[0:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/generative-adversarial-networks-gans?u=76281980&t=58)** This is an algorithm that produces novel output based on experience with training data.
>
> **[1:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/generative-adversarial-networks-gans?u=76281980&t=64)** So you show it a whole bunch of information, like a bunch of pictures, and it produces something that is inspired by those other ones, maybe with some kind of random or evolutionary variation on it, and it outputs that.
>
> **[1:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/generative-adversarial-networks-gans?u=76281980&t=78)** Now, the most common approach here is what's called a deconvolutional neural network.
>
> **[1:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/generative-adversarial-networks-gans?u=76281980&t=84)** But the output from this network is then sent to a separate network.
>
> **[1:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/generative-adversarial-networks-gans?u=76281980&t=90)** This is a discriminative network, or a discriminator, and this is an algorithm that attempts to distinguish the generated output from non-generated output.
>
> **[1:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/generative-adversarial-networks-gans?u=76281980&t=100)** So it's also seen a whole lot of real paintings, and it tries to tell the ones that a computer created versus the ones that the humans created.
>
> **[1:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/generative-adversarial-networks-gans?u=76281980&t=110)** And the most common approach here is what's called a convolutional neural network, which is frequently used for analyzing visual data.
>
> **[1:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/generative-adversarial-networks-gans?u=76281980&t=118)** And so you have these two networks, the generator and the discriminator, that are in competition with each other.
>
> **[2:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/generative-adversarial-networks-gans?u=76281980&t=126)** And it's a little bit like when you're playing soccer and you're going for that penalty kick.
>
> **[2:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/generative-adversarial-networks-gans?u=76281980&t=131)** And you've got the offense that is trying to get the ball into that, and the defense that is trying to stop the ball and keep it out.
>
> **[2:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/generative-adversarial-networks-gans?u=76281980&t=138)** It is a competition.
>
> **[2:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/generative-adversarial-networks-gans?u=76281980&t=141)** And one of the interesting things about competition, as we all know, it makes things advance.
>
> **[2:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/generative-adversarial-networks-gans?u=76281980&t=147)** So there's a progression.
>
> **[2:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/generative-adversarial-networks-gans?u=76281980&t=148)** The generator gets better and better at creating data that fools the discriminator.
>
> **[2:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/generative-adversarial-networks-gans?u=76281980&t=155)** At the same time, the discriminator gets better and better at spotting the generated data.
>
> **[2:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/generative-adversarial-networks-gans?u=76281980&t=160)** So it's kind of like an arms race, they each improve.
>
> **[2:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/generative-adversarial-networks-gans?u=76281980&t=165)** And what you get is data that's more realistic.
>
> **[2:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/generative-adversarial-networks-gans?u=76281980&t=168)** Like for instance, every one of these photos here off to the side, these are not real people.
>
> **[2:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/generative-adversarial-networks-gans?u=76281980&t=174)** These are portraits that were generated by a generative adversarial network, and you can see it's really effective.
>
> **[3:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/generative-adversarial-networks-gans?u=76281980&t=183)** Now, there are a number of use cases, and I'll start with what you might call the legitimate use cases.
>
> **[3:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/generative-adversarial-networks-gans?u=76281980&t=190)** And that is, you can use these generative adversarial networks, or GANs, to upscale images and videos.
>
> **[3:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/generative-adversarial-networks-gans?u=76281980&t=197)** Say you got a low-resolution photo or a low-resolution digital video, it can fill in the details enough to make it so everything is high resolutions 4K.
>
> **[3:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/generative-adversarial-networks-gans?u=76281980&t=208)** And it can be used to create images for fashion and for design visualizations, like these shoes.
>
> **[3:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/generative-adversarial-networks-gans?u=76281980&t=215)** I don't even know if these are real shoes.
>
> **[3:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/generative-adversarial-networks-gans?u=76281980&t=217)** A GAN could create products that look real and images that look real.
>
> **[3:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/generative-adversarial-networks-gans?u=76281980&t=224)** They're also useful for creating realistic animated movies.
>
> **[3:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/generative-adversarial-networks-gans?u=76281980&t=227)** Several very large-budget Hollywood movies have included extremely realistic animation that was created using GANs.
>
> **[3:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/generative-adversarial-networks-gans?u=76281980&t=238)** And then they can also be used in various kinds of scientific simulations, and even in molecular research.
>
> **[4:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/generative-adversarial-networks-gans?u=76281980&t=244)** So this creative process that generates novel data and then sends it to a discriminator that tries to distinguish between the two, so the generator has to get its game together, very productive in a lot of ways.
>
> **[4:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/generative-adversarial-networks-gans?u=76281980&t=262)** That said, there are some trade-offs and potential problems.
>
> **[4:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/generative-adversarial-networks-gans?u=76281980&t=267)** Two of the most important that are closely related are called mode collapse and instability.
>
> **[4:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/generative-adversarial-networks-gans?u=76281980&t=273)** And mode collapse means that the generator has figured out one particular way to fool the discriminator, and so it settles on this limited output, and it really gives up all the other opportunities.
>
> **[4:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/generative-adversarial-networks-gans?u=76281980&t=287)** It loses diversity in its output, so it gets a high rate of passing the test, but it runs the risk of generating just the same two or three things over and over and over again.
>
> **[5:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/generative-adversarial-networks-gans?u=76281980&t=302)** Instability is closely related.
>
> **[5:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/generative-adversarial-networks-gans?u=76281980&t=304)** It turns out that generative adversarial networks are very sensitive to the precise tuning of the parameters.
>
> **[5:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/generative-adversarial-networks-gans?u=76281980&t=310)** So for instance, if the discriminator is too weak, it doesn't know how to say no to things, it's easy to trick, and the generator never improves.
>
> **[5:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/generative-adversarial-networks-gans?u=76281980&t=319)** On the other hand, if the discriminator is too strong and it rejects everything, well, the generator gets no useful feedback, and again, doesn't know how to improve.
>
> **[5:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/generative-adversarial-networks-gans?u=76281980&t=328)** And there are a number of other parameters that affect the interplay of these two.
>
> **[5:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/generative-adversarial-networks-gans?u=76281980&t=334)** And it turns out that the adversarial relationship between the generator and the discriminator is both the strength and the weakness of this approach.
>
> **[5:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/generative-adversarial-networks-gans?u=76281980&t=345)** The adversarial relationship runs the risk of making progress towards better output, very non-linear.
>
> **[5:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/generative-adversarial-networks-gans?u=76281980&t=353)** So maybe nothing happens for a long time, then it jumps up, and it plateaus again.
>
> **[5:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/generative-adversarial-networks-gans?u=76281980&t=357)** And it also makes it unpredictable.
>
> **[5:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/generative-adversarial-networks-gans?u=76281980&t=359)** For that reason, as productive as GANs have been, people have tried to apply some other generative models.
>
> **[6:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/generative-adversarial-networks-gans?u=76281980&t=368)** So for instance, the transformer models that are central to GPT.
>
> **[6:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/generative-adversarial-networks-gans?u=76281980&t=374)** Now, these models have found to be more stable and more consistent because they don't use the adversarial approach of GANs.
>
> **[6:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/generative-adversarial-networks-gans?u=76281980&t=383)** Also, transformer models, because they originally developed with language, they're very good with language, and they're good with multimodal models.
>
> **[6:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/generative-adversarial-networks-gans?u=76281980&t=391)** So text and images and audio and video, any of those work.
>
> **[6:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/generative-adversarial-networks-gans?u=76281980&t=397)** One of the other benefits is that transformer models have long-range context.
>
> **[6:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/generative-adversarial-networks-gans?u=76281980&t=402)** I mean, you can feed 100 pages of text into them.
>
> **[6:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/generative-adversarial-networks-gans?u=76281980&t=405)** It'll remember all of it, and it can connect everything.
>
> **[6:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/generative-adversarial-networks-gans?u=76281980&t=407)** Same thing with video and images.
>
> **[6:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/generative-adversarial-networks-gans?u=76281980&t=409)** You can give it a lot of information, and it understands all of that context, and it can work better in that situation.
>
> **[6:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/generative-adversarial-networks-gans?u=76281980&t=416)** Now, the trade off, of course, is that transformer models require very large data sets.
>
> **[7:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/generative-adversarial-networks-gans?u=76281980&t=422)** Again, most generative models are known for sucking in the entire internet, and they require very extensive computation, at least to get trained and up and running.
>
> **[7:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/generative-adversarial-networks-gans?u=76281980&t=432)** And also, as is well known, transformer models are sometimes prone to hallucinations and just making things up.
>
> **[7:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/generative-adversarial-networks-gans?u=76281980&t=439)** That happens less with generative adversarial models.
>
> **[7:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/generative-adversarial-networks-gans?u=76281980&t=442)** And so, you have these trade-offs here.
>
> **[7:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/generative-adversarial-networks-gans?u=76281980&t=446)** Another approach is diffusion models.
>
> **[7:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/generative-adversarial-networks-gans?u=76281980&t=450)** If you think about DALL-E, Midjourney, and Stable Diffusion that are used to generate AI images like this, they work through this unusual process of taking the original data, and they kind of go backwards.
>
> **[7:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/generative-adversarial-networks-gans?u=76281980&t=463)** They add a lot of noise to the data until it's pure noise, and then they try to remove noise gradually to get back to something that looks identifiable.
>
> **[7:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/generative-adversarial-networks-gans?u=76281980&t=471)** And it's a peculiar process, but what it does is it ends up with image generation that is very stable and very high quality.
>
> **[8:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/generative-adversarial-networks-gans?u=76281980&t=481)** In fact, for image and video generation, this is the state of the art at this exact moment.
>
> **[8:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/generative-adversarial-networks-gans?u=76281980&t=486)** But as with other AI methods, it tends to be computationally very intensive.
>
> **[8:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/generative-adversarial-networks-gans?u=76281980&t=491)** Again, large data sets, lots of computation, and then relatively slow compared to things like generative adversarial networks.
>
> **[8:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/generative-adversarial-networks-gans?u=76281980&t=498)** On the other hand, everybody knows that there are some potential problems with this.
>
> **[8:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/generative-adversarial-networks-gans?u=76281980&t=503)** GANs make it possible to create fake images, fake videos, fake audio, fake text, and even fake data sets.
>
> **[8:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/generative-adversarial-networks-gans?u=76281980&t=512)** And then you can also use it to create fake social media profiles and posts, and to place fake phone calls, send fake text messages, and so on.
>
> **[8:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/generative-adversarial-networks-gans?u=76281980&t=522)** It actually becomes really difficult sometimes to know what's real and what's not.
>
> **[8:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/generative-adversarial-networks-gans?u=76281980&t=526)** It's easy to take an image of one person, and then create a video of them saying whatever you want them to say in their own voice.
>
> **[8:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/generative-adversarial-networks-gans?u=76281980&t=533)** And so there is a very serious, problematic element to this.
>
> **[8:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/generative-adversarial-networks-gans?u=76281980&t=539)** That doesn't mean we shouldn't have GANs.
>
> **[9:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/generative-adversarial-networks-gans?u=76281980&t=541)** GANs are able to do so much of the magic of data science.
>
> **[9:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/generative-adversarial-networks-gans?u=76281980&t=545)** And I like to think that with great promise, the ability to have computers do things that we just didn't even think were possible, comes great risk and a great need to be mindful of how this is used.
>
> **[9:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/generative-adversarial-networks-gans?u=76281980&t=558)** And so there are laws that exist in certain locations that ban the use of GANs to generate, for instance, fake images of actual people in a kind of defamation.
>
> **[9:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/generative-adversarial-networks-gans?u=76281980&t=571)** But there needs to be a broader societal discussion about what is acceptable, what is not, and what the guardrails are to keep this particular technology in line while allowing us to benefit from its amazing abilities.

#### Reinforcement learning
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/reinforcement-learning?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/reinforcement-learning?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] Perhaps you've seen the video of the Atlas Robot by Boston Dynamics, not as anthropomorphic as this one, but still bipedal, running through a parkour course and doing back flips.
>
> **[0:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/reinforcement-learning?u=76281980&t=13)** It's amazing.
>
> **[0:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/reinforcement-learning?u=76281980&t=14)** It's a moment that is incredible, both for its technical accomplishments as well as for its ability to make me feel even more discoordinated than usual.
>
> **[0:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/reinforcement-learning?u=76281980&t=24)** But reinforcement learning is the key to a whole realm of extraordinary accomplishments in data science.
>
> **[0:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/reinforcement-learning?u=76281980&t=31)** So for instance, when a computer algorithm is able to play chess and go, games that people thought were way too complicated for computers, and not only did they learn to play it, but they beat the best people in the world.
>
> **[0:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/reinforcement-learning?u=76281980&t=44)** Or self-driving cars that can keep themselves between the lanes and get you across the country.
>
> **[0:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/reinforcement-learning?u=76281980&t=50)** Or stock market trading, where algorithms are designed to find optimal times to buy and sell certain stocks at certain amounts to maximize the overall profit.
>
> **[1:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/reinforcement-learning?u=76281980&t=61)** Or one of the more interesting applications, because it's life and death, is healthcare where reinforcement learning can be used to determine dosages for medication, dynamic treatment regimes, or DTRs, for chronic illness, planning and conducting clinical trials and a whole host of other outcomes.
>
> **[1:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/reinforcement-learning?u=76281980&t=80)** The basic principles of reinforcement learning are pretty simple.
>
> **[1:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/reinforcement-learning?u=76281980&t=85)** You start by setting up the situation.
>
> **[1:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/reinforcement-learning?u=76281980&t=88)** You need to give the algorithm the rules and constraints.
>
> **[1:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/reinforcement-learning?u=76281980&t=91)** It needs to know what's allowed and when it's offside.
>
> **[1:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/reinforcement-learning?u=76281980&t=95)** And then you need to have discreet steps in time where you can measure both what it has done and you can measure the reward function or Q.
>
> **[1:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/reinforcement-learning?u=76281980&t=104)** Q is the expected value of the total reward from the current starting point, which is why one of the most common approaches to reinforcement learning is called Q learning.
>
> **[1:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/reinforcement-learning?u=76281980&t=114)** So you have to be able to measure or put numbers on the progress that you're doing.
>
> **[1:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/reinforcement-learning?u=76281980&t=119)** And if you can have that reward function, then you can then put the algorithm into play.
>
> **[2:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/reinforcement-learning?u=76281980&t=127)** And what you're trying to do is create what's called a policy map, where that's the probability of taking a particular action when in a given state or condition.
>
> **[2:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/reinforcement-learning?u=76281980&t=136)** And then you have these twin ideas of exploration, which means the algorithm is going to try lots and lots of different possible behaviors, make lots of different choices at each given point, go in every direction and see how well it works.
>
> **[2:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/reinforcement-learning?u=76281980&t=154)** And then exploitation.
>
> **[2:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/reinforcement-learning?u=76281980&t=156)** And in reinforcement learning, this is a good thing.
>
> **[2:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/reinforcement-learning?u=76281980&t=159)** It means to exploit the things that it has already learned to continue its progress.
>
> **[2:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/reinforcement-learning?u=76281980&t=165)** So that's how you can assemble the policy map and that's the general process in very broad strokes of how reinforcement learning works.
>
> **[2:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/reinforcement-learning?u=76281980&t=175)** Or if you want something slightly more specific, you'll come across the acronym SARSA, which stands for state, action, reward, then the subsequent state and the subsequent action.
>
> **[3:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/reinforcement-learning?u=76281980&t=188)** This is an iterative algorithm that is used in a kind of policy learning called Markov decision process, which is very, very common within reinforcement learning.
>
> **[3:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/reinforcement-learning?u=76281980&t=200)** On the other hand, one of the major challenges in reinforcement learning is what's called the credit assignment problem, and that is exactly who are you going to give that gold star to.
>
> **[3:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/reinforcement-learning?u=76281980&t=209)** This has to do with the gap in time between the action and the feedback.
>
> **[3:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/reinforcement-learning?u=76281980&t=215)** You want that to be as short as possible to make the reinforcement unambiguous.
>
> **[3:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/reinforcement-learning?u=76281980&t=220)** But if you're working on a self-driving car, for instance, you want it to measure mile by mile or maybe even foot by foot, so you can give it immediate feedback instead of just a yes or no on whether it's successfully got somebody across the country.
>
> **[3:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/reinforcement-learning?u=76281980&t=234)** Now, that's an absurd example, but for instance, with some medical interventions like changing a person's medications or trying a new procedure, there can be a difficult period of adaptation or a recovery period before the eventual improvement is manifested.
>
> **[4:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/reinforcement-learning?u=76281980&t=250)** And by the way, this is similar in concept to what is called the attribution problem in online marketing, where you're trying to determine exactly which factors led, for example, to an eventual purchase, and that's a major challenge.
>
> **[4:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/reinforcement-learning?u=76281980&t=266)** It's knowing where exactly, again, where are you going to give the credit?
>
> **[4:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/reinforcement-learning?u=76281980&t=269)** Where are you going to put that gold star?
>
> **[4:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/reinforcement-learning?u=76281980&t=272)** Now another interesting challenge in reinforcement learning is initializing, where to start 'cause you can provide the algorithm with specific examples to learn from.
>
> **[4:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/reinforcement-learning?u=76281980&t=283)** You can have it watch thousands or millions of chess games.
>
> **[4:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/reinforcement-learning?u=76281980&t=286)** You can have it get all this data from medical records.
>
> **[4:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/reinforcement-learning?u=76281980&t=289)** There's a lot that you can do to get it set up.
>
> **[4:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/reinforcement-learning?u=76281980&t=291)** On the other hand, you can also have these quote/unquote "naive situations" where all you do is give it the rules.
>
> **[4:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/reinforcement-learning?u=76281980&t=298)** You simply tell it what the rules of chess are and it learns on its own how to progress.
>
> **[5:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/reinforcement-learning?u=76281980&t=302)** There are fascinating examples of watching virtual robots in games learning how to move themselves with no instructions at all except for the basic laws of physics.
>
> **[5:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/reinforcement-learning?u=76281980&t=314)** And sometimes you end up with peculiar solutions, but they're effective.
>
> **[5:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/reinforcement-learning?u=76281980&t=318)** And so this is one of the choices you get to make in terms of setting up your reinforcement learning approach.
>
> **[5:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/reinforcement-learning?u=76281980&t=325)** Now, if you'd like to learn more about this topic, because there is a ton more that you could learn, I highly recommend the excellent course, [[Reinforcement Learning Foundations]] by Khaulat Abdulhakeem.
>
> **[5:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/reinforcement-learning?u=76281980&t=335)** What this shows you is one method for doing some of the extraordinary magic that is associated with data science in terms of teaching programs, machines, what the goal is, and then letting them figure out on their own, have their own developmental sequence in terms of getting to it.
>
> **[5:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/reinforcement-learning?u=76281980&t=353)** It's an extraordinarily flexible and creative approach to a lot of very challenging problems and one of the things that makes data science so useful.

>
> **[2:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/techniques-for-creating-interpretable-models?u=76281980&t=143)** That includes, for instance, regression with interactions where you no longer know immediately how it's going to affect things, or random forests, that is, large collections of decision trees, where you could visualize an individual tree, but knowing how they're all going to act is a little more complicated.
>
> **[2:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/techniques-for-creating-interpretable-models?u=76281980&t=164)** Or machine learning algorithms like support vector machines, and then, of course, neural networks is our really best possible example of a complex and opaque, difficult-to-understand procedure, but one that works very, very well.
>
> **[3:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/techniques-for-creating-interpretable-models?u=76281980&t=180)** Now, what I'm saying here in that some are easier to interpret and some are harder to interpret, it's not exactly the same thing as Occam's Razor, where the simplest explanation is taken as the one that's most likely to be true, and that is a theory that I strongly support, and I encourage people to use the simplest method wherever possible.
>
> **[3:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/techniques-for-creating-interpretable-models?u=76281980&t=202)** Also, this easy and hard to interpret isn't quite like the less is more minimalism of architect Mies van der Rohe that I love so much.
>
> **[3:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/techniques-for-creating-interpretable-models?u=76281980&t=212)** Instead, it's a little more like going from a black box, that's where it's hard to know exactly how the data is processed.
>
> **[3:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/techniques-for-creating-interpretable-models?u=76281980&t=219)** Neural networks use a lot of very non-linear transformations of the data, and it's hard to predict how the input data will combine for the output.
>
> **[3:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/techniques-for-creating-interpretable-models?u=76281980&t=229)** Well, a black box, while it can be extremely effective, can be hard to interpret and hard to apply in a new situation, and it's moving to a glass box, a clear box.
>
> **[4:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/techniques-for-creating-interpretable-models?u=76281980&t=241)** These are methods where you can see how the data is processed, even if there's a lot going on in there, and theoretically it's easy to predict the outcomes from the inputs.
>
> **[4:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/techniques-for-creating-interpretable-models?u=76281980&t=250)** And so when a clear method and easy-to-interpret one works, there should be a preference for that.
>
> **[4:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/techniques-for-creating-interpretable-models?u=76281980&t=259)** And, of course, one of the really intriguing benefits of using generative AI models in any kind of data science work is that even though the method itself might be very complex and opaque, the generative AI is able to offer a narrative that explains itself.
>
> **[4:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/techniques-for-creating-interpretable-models?u=76281980&t=278)** It actually can write it out in paragraphs, it can talk to you out loud, and it's able to offer an explanation that draws on its knowledge of the very broad context in which it's operating, and that opens new possibilities for interpretability.
>
> **[4:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/techniques-for-creating-interpretable-models?u=76281980&t=295)** On the other hand, there's also the idea that there is necessary complexity.
>
> **[5:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/techniques-for-creating-interpretable-models?u=76281980&t=300)** Circuit boards are complicated, but they need to be complicated in order to accomplish their purpose.
>
> **[5:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/techniques-for-creating-interpretable-models?u=76281980&t=307)** But ultimately, your analysis is like a map that helps your organization get from point A, that's where you currently are, to point B, that's your goal, your intended outcome, and, when possible, choose a method that helps you best understand how to get there so you can reach your goal, so you can deal with any potential setbacks, and so you can know when you're there.
>
> **[5:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/techniques-for-creating-interpretable-models?u=76281980&t=331)** It helps you work more efficiently and more effectively when you are able to interpret your algorithms.

#### Delivering actionable insights
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/delivering-actionable-insights?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/delivering-actionable-insights?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Narrator] If you're working in a startup or really any entrepreneurial or organizational setting, then you know that your work is all about getting results.
>
> **[0:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/delivering-actionable-insights?u=76281980&t=10)** And that brings up something that I mentioned earlier in this course I want to mention again, from one of my heroes, the American psychologist and philosopher, William James, who said, "My thinking is first and last, and always for the sake of my doing."
>
> **[0:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/delivering-actionable-insights?u=76281980&t=25)** His point is that human cognition is designed to fulfill goals to help us reach particular ends.
>
> **[0:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/delivering-actionable-insights?u=76281980&t=33)** And I like to summarize that and apply it towards data science with this thought, that data and data science is for doing.
>
> **[0:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/delivering-actionable-insights?u=76281980&t=42)** It exists to help us do things.
>
> **[0:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/delivering-actionable-insights?u=76281980&t=45)** And the reason we do these projects is to help us accomplish things that are important to us.
>
> **[0:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/delivering-actionable-insights?u=76281980&t=51)** Remember when you did the project, there was a goal, there was some motivation.
>
> **[0:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/delivering-actionable-insights?u=76281980&t=55)** What motivated the project?
>
> **[0:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/delivering-actionable-insights?u=76281980&t=58)** What sorts of things did you stick up on the wall?
>
> **[1:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/delivering-actionable-insights?u=76281980&t=61)** These are questions you wanted answered.
>
> **[1:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/delivering-actionable-insights?u=76281980&t=63)** Why was the project conducted?
>
> **[1:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/delivering-actionable-insights?u=76281980&t=65)** The goal is usually to direct some kind of particular action.
>
> **[1:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/delivering-actionable-insights?u=76281980&t=68)** Should we open a new store over here?
>
> **[1:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/delivering-actionable-insights?u=76281980&t=70)** Should we reduce the price over here?
>
> **[1:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/delivering-actionable-insights?u=76281980&t=72)** Should we partner up with this other organization over here?
>
> **[1:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/delivering-actionable-insights?u=76281980&t=75)** And your analysis should be able to guide those actions.
>
> **[1:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/delivering-actionable-insights?u=76281980&t=80)** And so can you remember what those clear questions were?
>
> **[1:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/delivering-actionable-insights?u=76281980&t=84)** And can you give a clear, well articulated and justifiable response to those questions, based on your data science project?
>
> **[1:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/delivering-actionable-insights?u=76281980&t=94)** When you do, there's a few things you want to keep in mind.
>
> **[1:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/delivering-actionable-insights?u=76281980&t=97)** You need to focus on things that are controllable.
>
> **[1:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/delivering-actionable-insights?u=76281980&t=100)** The analysis might say that companies founded in the 80s have greater success, but if you're founded in 2015, there's not much you can do about it.
>
> **[1:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/delivering-actionable-insights?u=76281980&t=108)** So focus on something that is under your control and try to make it something that's specific.
>
> **[1:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/delivering-actionable-insights?u=76281980&t=113)** Also, be practical.
>
> **[1:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/delivering-actionable-insights?u=76281980&t=115)** Think about the return on investment, or ROI.
>
> **[2:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/delivering-actionable-insights?u=76281980&t=120)** You need to work on things and give actions where the impact will be large enough to justify the efforts.
>
> **[2:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/delivering-actionable-insights?u=76281980&t=127)** Also, if you're giving recommendations to a client, make sure it's something that they're actually capable of doing.
>
> **[2:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/delivering-actionable-insights?u=76281980&t=133)** And then also, you want to build up, you want to have sequential steps.
>
> **[2:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/delivering-actionable-insights?u=76281980&t=138)** You want to make a small recommendation, carry through on it, and then build on it as you see the results of each earlier step.
>
> **[2:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/delivering-actionable-insights?u=76281980&t=147)** The data science project is designed to fulfill all of these requirements in a way that the benefits will be visible to the client as you help them find an answer to their question.
>
> **[2:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/delivering-actionable-insights?u=76281980&t=160)** And if you can get that done, then you've done exactly what you meant to do when you started in data science, and that is worthy of an office celebration.
>
> **[2:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/delivering-actionable-insights?u=76281980&t=170)** So congratulations.

> [!info]- Semantic Content

>
> **[0:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/next-steps?u=76281980&t=24)** I haven't been able to go into detail on these topics, but that's okay.

>

>

>
> **[1:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/next-steps?u=76281980&t=74)** Learn more about data science related fields like [[Decision Intelligence]].
>
> **[1:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/next-steps?u=76281980&t=78)** That's an interdisciplinary field that combines data science, AI, social science, and decision theory to optimize decision-making by integrating human expertise with data-driven insights, with modeling, and even with automation.
>
> **[1:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/next-steps?u=76281980&t=93)** And then get information on how people work and the elements that are most important in fields like marketing or nonprofits or healthcare or education or whatever is of greatest use and interest to you.
>
> **[1:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/next-steps?u=76281980&t=108)** Also get connected with the actual people in data science.
>
> **[1:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/next-steps?u=76281980&t=113)** Go to conferences.
>
> **[1:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/next-steps?u=76281980&t=114)** There's so many different ways you can do this.
>
> **[1:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/next-steps?u=76281980&t=117)** For example, you can go to large national general topic conferences like the Strata Data conferences or one of my favorites, ODSC, for the Open Data Science Conference.
>

>
> **[2:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/next-steps?u=76281980&t=132)** There's one that's going to be near you that you can go to, or maybe you have a specialized topic like for instance, I've gone to the Marketing Analytics and Data Science or MADS conference, which very specifically focuses on data science within this particular marketing realm, or where you live, you may have local events.
>
> **[2:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/next-steps?u=76281980&t=153)** I'm in Utah and each year we have the Silicon Slopes Tech Summit, which has tracks focused on artificial intelligence, machine learning, and data science.
>
> **[2:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/data-science-foundations-fundamentals-24591071/next-steps?u=76281980&t=163)** But remember all of this, all of this is fundamentally about people and the way that you can both better understand the people in the world around you and turn that understanding into something of value for the people you work with.
